**First draft attempt:**

I have served the King of Thronegate for three decades, and my nightmares have always been about the day the universe finally tried to kill him. Not because I feared for him—never that—but because I feared what he would become in response. I am Leon, the thirty-seventh court wizard of the line of Blake, and my bloodline has stood beside that impossible throne since before the Awakening, since before the Stasis, since before the galaxy learned to tremble. And I can tell you, with absolute certainty, that the thing I witnessed last week was not a battle. It was not a war. It was a lesson in the mathematics of absolute, uncrossable power, and I am still bleeding from the brain trying to comprehend it.

The omniverse had united. Not a resistance like the old days, not a scattered coalition of arrogant gods who thought they had found a loophole. This was everything. Every conceivable universe, dimension, plane, layer, thread, and pocket reality had pooled their resources, their gods, their concepts, their very essence into a single undertaking. They had stripped existence bare. Billions of universes had voluntarily collapsed themselves into fuel for a single weapon, the Omnicide Lance. Entire pantheons had merged their souls into a unified consciousness strong enough to wield it. The survivors—what was left of the multiverse—huddled in a pocket realm that they had reinforced with the last scraps of causality, and they aimed the Lance at Godric with a hope that was equal parts insanity and desperation.

I stood at Godric's side on a viewing platform forged from his boredom. He had created it a moment before, just for me. He stood, hands clasped behind his back, his salt-and-pepper beard catching the light of a dying star he'd repositioned for aesthetics. He watched the amassing weaponry with the expression of a man waiting for his toast to pop.

“You know they’ve sacrificed everything, right?” I said. My voice came out steadier than I felt. “Whole civilizations have erased themselves just to contribute a volt of power to that thing.”

“I know,” Godric said. “It’s sweet, really. They’ve been planning this for millennia. I let them grow, excluded them from Gent’s casual omnipresent cleanup, gave them the privacy to scheme. I even helped, indirectly. I’d gently nudge a quantum fluctuation here, a brilliant idea there. I wanted to see what they’d come up with.”

He turned his head, and his smile was the warm smile of a father. “They call it the Omnicide Lance. It’s designed to erase me from the omniverse retroactively, by unraveling the concept of my existence at the moment of my birth. It’s quite clever.”

“And?” I pressed.

“And I’ve already perfected it,” he said. “The weakness paradox. Every time they planned, every time they thought ‘this is the one weakness,’ my passive defenses absorbed the concept, granted me mastery, and made me immune. I’ve had perfect command of the Omnicide Lance for longer than its creators have existed. I could deny its very idea to them if I wanted. But that would ruin the show.”

He then did something that made my bowels loosen. He rolled up his sleeve and pointed to a spot on his forearm. There, on the surface of his skin, among the microscopic layer of dead cells, was a single cell that had a microscopic crack. It was nothing—less than nothing, a flaw so small that only his omniscience could perceive it. He had willed it there.

“I created that crack,” he said. “A dead skin cell. The weakest, most expendable part of my physical form. Now, listen carefully: I’ve ordered Gent to stand down. My sentient passive aura—the one that is merely my excess metaphysical body heat—could erase that Lance and its entire army with an infinitesimal fraction of his attention, and he’s the weakest of my auras. I’ve also deactivated my infinite passive shields, my conceptual negations, my retrocausal protections. If that Lance hits me, it will strike that dead cell, and it will widen that crack. Not because it’s powerful enough, but because I am allowing it.”

“Why?” I whispered.

“Because I’m curious what my immune system will do. Nothing has ever been able to hurt me, not even a little. Not since the Stasis. My body has never needed to react. I want to see it try.”

He winked at me. “Also, I’m bored.”

The Lance fired.

Now, before I tell you what actually happened, let me tell you the story my mind wanted to believe. In that fraction of a moment between the Lance’s impact and the body’s response, I wanted to imagine that the resistance saw the crack widen. That they saw a jagged line appear on the dead skin cell of the god they had sacrificed everything to kill. That they erupted in a cacophony of joy, tears streaming down faces that had never known hope, shouting that they had finally, finally drawn blood. That the unified consciousness of the pantheons wept with relief, and the last survivors clutched each other, believing that the tyrant could be hurt, could be killed, could be stopped. That for one glorious, shining second, the omniverse celebrated their impossible victory.

But that never happened.

Not a single atom of that joy ever existed. Because before the crack could even properly form, before the Lance’s energy could travel the distance of a Planck length, Godric’s immune system reacted. Not reacted—it pre-reacted. It had already sensed the “injury” before the Lance was even conceived, thanks to retrocausal defense mechanisms that were among Godric’s most basic passive abilities, and it had been waiting, coiled, for this exact moment.

The first thing that happened was the dead cell repaired itself. Not with mundane keratin, but with a substance that was the conceptual opposite of harm—a material forged from the very idea of inviolability, something that could not be scratched by anything, including the concept of scratching. And then, because the immune system is paranoid, it replaced every single cell in Godric’s body, dead or alive, with this new substance. In the time it takes me to blink, his entire physical form was now made of Absolute Inviolability 2.0.

That was the mildest response.

Next, the “antigen recognition” system kicked in. The body identified the concept of “being hurt” as a foreign pathogen. It then proceeded to purge that concept from all of time and space. The Omnicide Lance, and every weapon that had ever been forged with the intent to harm Godric, was retroactively un-created. The attackers didn’t just lose their weapon; they lost the memory of its creation, the scientific principles behind it, and the very inspiration that had driven them. They stood in the void, suddenly holding nothing, their minds blank, their purpose erased. Then, because the immune system deemed them carriers of the “harm” pathogen, it proceeded to eliminate them. Not kill—eliminate. Their bodies unraveled from the cellular level upward, their souls unmade, their histories dissolved, leaving not even a psychic echo. I watched as the fused pantheon-consciousness shrieked across twelve dimensions and was swallowed by an antibody made of frozen time.

This was still among the mild reactions.

Then the redundancy system activated. Godric, you see, has infinite identical backups of himself, each a full, perfect Godric, existing in a recursive hierarchy that defies description. For an injury to be truly registered, every single one of those backups—including the infinite backups of each backup, and the infinite backups of those—must experience the exact same injury at the exact same instant. The system performed this check in negative time and found the condition unmet. Logically, the injury never occurred. Yet, despite this, the immune system still decided to trigger a full upgrade cascade across the entire recursive lattice. Every copy of Godric’s biology across the infinite recursion spontaneously ascended, gaining new invulnerabilities that dwarfed their previous states, and then they cross-referenced their upgrades, merging them into a unified defensive lattice that was exponentially more impregnable than the sum of its infinite parts. It was like giving a man a paper cut and responding by encasing him in a universe made of unbreakable armor, then reinforcing that universe with infinite layers of itself.

And still, the immune system was not satisfied.

It triggered a “fever.” The localized area around the “injury” suddenly reached a temperature that was not merely infinite in Celsius, but was the theoretical maximum heat of all conceivable thermodynamics compressed into a singularity of pure agony. This heat instantly vaporized the entire omniverse—every universe, every plane, every pocket dimension that had hosted the resistance, and a few that hadn’t. They were all caught in the splash. Only I survived, because Godric had placed his hand on my shoulder, and that touch was a bubble of absolute protection that nothing, not even his own fever, could breach. I still felt the heat, though. I felt it as a distant, childlike warmth, like a memory of a sunbeam, and that was somehow more terrifying than agony.

The final layer of the mild reaction was an evolutionary burst. Godric’s immune cells, which had been dormant for twenty-five thousand years, underwent a hyper-accelerated evolution that normally would take from the birth of time to its heat death, compressed into an instant. They became sentient, omnipotent, and omnipresent. They then decided to “improve” Godric’s entire body to prevent any future injuries. They added new sensory organelles that could detect ill intent before it even formed into a thought, and responded by preemptively annihilating the source. They wove a new passive defense that was akin to the omniscience of the universe itself, but stronger, because it was part of Godric. They then, for good measure, linked themselves to the dormant auras—Gent and his countless siblings—and shared their upgrades, effectively making the already unbearable Gent obsolete by comparison.

And this was all from a cracked dead skin cell.

I became aware that some of this was because the weakness paradox had been triggered. By willing the crack, Godric had technically committed an act of self-harm, which contradicted his accumulated immunities. The omniverse, in its panicked apology, had overcompensated by further amplifying his already infinite stats. His amplification rate, which was already beyond incalculable, received a permanent boost of a factor so large that the mathematics required to express it would be larger than the omniverse itself. The omniverse also granted him several new “apology” powers: one of them allowed him to unmake the concept of “offense” from any being, another granted him perfect, effortless control over the concept of “restraint” (which, coming from a guy who accidentally destroys galaxies, was rich).

Godric watched all of this with the same expression a parent wears when their toddler proudly presents a scribble. He looked at his forearm, where the crack had been, and saw only a shimmering, impervious plane that now glowed with a soft, gentle light—the light of infinite safety.

“Well,” he said, patting his arm. “That was adorable. My immune system is so dramatic. It’s like a puppy that thinks a shoelace is a threat and barks at it until the entire neighborhood is awake.”

He turned to me, and his eyes were still kind, still warm. “Did you see how it replaced every cell? I didn’t even need that. But it’s trying so hard.”

I couldn’t speak. My legs had given out. I was kneeling on the platform, my hands clutching my chest, my heart skipping beats in sheer existential dread. The omniverse—the entire omniverse—had been wiped out. Every single being that had rallied, every universe that had sacrificed, every god and mortal and concept that had hoped for a single moment of victory. They were gone. Not just dead, but erased across all time, all memory, all possibility. And the only reason they had ever gotten close was because Godric allowed it, for a joke, for a curiosity. And even that “closeness” was a falsehood—the injury never actually happened. It was a staged play with no audience except me.

“Oh,” Godric said, as if remembering something. “I should fix that.”

He didn’t move. He didn’t gesture. He just decided, and in zero seconds—less, because time had no meaning—the entire omniverse was restored. Every universe that had collapsed was re-inflated, every soul that had been dissolved was reconstituted, every memory was re-uploaded exactly as it had been before the Lance. The resistance found themselves back in their pocket realm, with their weapons and their hope, completely unaware that they had just been annihilated, unmade, and resurrected. They would go on plotting, unaware that their greatest triumph was a scripted farce.

I, however, remembered all of it. Godric made sure I did. He looked down at me, still smiling, still fatherly, and said, “Are you all right, Leon? You look pale.”

“You… you let them hurt you,” I stammered. “Just to see what would happen.”

“Yes. And it was quite informative. My body is even more invincible now. I don’t think they could hurt me if they tried, not unless I let them again. Which I might. It’s fun to watch the puppy play.”

He reached down and helped me to my feet. His touch was gentle, and my terror spiked, but it was also comforting. That’s the curse of serving Godric: you love him. He is the warmest, kindest ruler you could ever hope for. He would carry your groceries and attend your child’s naming ceremony. And simultaneously, he could, with less effort than a thought, erase your entire lineage from the annals of reality and not even notice he’d done it.

As I stood, trembling, I realized the full, sickening unfairness of it all. They had sacrificed everything—their universes, their gods, their existence—to scratch a single dead cell, and he had willed even that into being. And in response, he had become infinitely more powerful, more invulnerable, more untouchable than he had been a moment before. The gap, already an infinite chasm, had been multiplicatively expanded by a factor that would require an infinite number of infinities to describe. They had thrown the kitchen sink at the ocean and the ocean had become more ocean.

Worst of all, I could hear the drowsy stirring of the other auras—the siblings of Gent. Gent, the weakest, had been held back, but I felt a flicker of a much larger presence, a sentient passive shield that could devour the concept of attack and still be hungry, roll over in its dormancy and go back to sleep, disappointed it wasn’t needed. Godric shushed them with a thought, and they quieted.

I walked back to the palace with him. On the way, he talked about the new recipe he wanted to try for dinner, and how proud he was of Gent for not disobeying, and how he might let the resistance try again in another thousand years, just to see if they could make his toe twitch.

He was genuinely happy. And I, his loyal court wizard, was trapped in a mind that would never stop screaming. I still serve him. I still love him. I have to. The alternative is to acknowledge that existence is a sandcastle built at the foot of an infinite, indifferent, and perversely loving storm. And I don’t have the courage to face that truth without the storm’s hand on my shoulder.

So I smile, and I make jokes, and I help him pick out new robes. And at night, when I close my eyes, I see that dead skin cell crack and the universe die. And I wonder, if he ever rolls his sleeve up again, will I be able to stand it?

The worst part? The very worst part? He would genuinely feel bad if he knew how much it hurt me. He would try to tone it down next time. But he can't, because he doesn't understand what "toning it down" means. He is the sun trying not to burn the ant, and the ant just has to cope with the fact that even a distant, loving sun can still blind you with its mere existence.

That’s the truth of Godric. The tyrant who isn't a tyrant. The god who loves mortals so much that he accidentally annihilates them with his version of a gentle caress. And I, his court wizard, am the luckiest, most terrified man in the omniverse.
</blockquote>

## ./prompts/prompt14_godric_intelligence.md

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.
- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.
- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called "customer satisfaction". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.
- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **maximum 3500 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.

**Style and Tone Requirements:**

- Write from **1st person POV** of Grim.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.
- Absolutely no censorship
- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.
- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. You must ensure that Godric always appears as the ultimate apex god predator, and he’s so overwhelmingly overpowered that his slightest thought can destroy the entire omniverse without him having to move a muscle. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.
- You must remember that Godric possesses absolute omniscience. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.
- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric’s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric’s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.
- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.
- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.
- Use fresh, specific language instead of clichés or idioms.
- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.
- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.
- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Real dialogue over exposition.
- Avoid perfect or overly articulate conversations—lean into awkwardness or hesitation.
- Limit adjectives and adverbs—prioritize strong nouns and verbs.
- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.
- Avoid AI tropes like “go home” “i know” “they didn’t know what to say” or “something in their eyes.” Be precise.
- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

This story happens 50,000 years after godric became king of thronegate.

Everyone knows that Godric is an overwhelmingly powerful king (that is a huge understatement, he's the ultimate god apex predator of everything). What not everyone knows is that Godric is actually very intelligent too, as his intelligence multiplies infinitely every Planck second. He also has absolute omniscience so it is literally impossible to have things unknown to him. He just genuinely prefers to appear as a simple friendly old father, close to his true mortal self a long time ago. In addition, his wisdom is also multiplying infinitely, and for someone like him, it's wiser to not use his overwhelming intelligence or there will be no problems to solve, no purpose in life that he cannot just solve instantly. This, however, makes some people perceive him wrongly. Write a story of a delegate who thought he could fool godric, and the consequence that follows. Grim, 25 years old, is Godric's court wizard.

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.
- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.
- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called "customer satisfaction". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.
- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **maximum 3500 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.

**Style and Tone Requirements:**

- Write from **1st person POV** of Gorm.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.
- Absolutely no censorship
- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.
- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. You must ensure that Godric always appears as the ultimate apex god predator, and he’s so overwhelmingly overpowered that his slightest thought can destroy the entire omniverse without him having to move a muscle. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.
- You must remember that Godric possesses absolute omniscience. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.
- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric’s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric’s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.
- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.
- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.
- Use fresh, specific language instead of clichés or idioms.
- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.
- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.
- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Real dialogue over exposition.
- Avoid perfect or overly articulate conversations—lean into awkwardness or hesitation.
- Limit adjectives and adverbs—prioritize strong nouns and verbs.
- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.
- Avoid AI tropes like “go home” “i know” “they didn’t know what to say” or “something in their eyes.” Be precise.
- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

This story takes place 80,000 years after Godric becomes the King of Thronegate. Throughout the years, Blake's descendants have served Godric as court wizard. Godric never actually needs their magical protection, healing, help, or anything that a typical court wizard typically provides. Godric’s court wizard’s magics are really potent and terrifying, especially since all of them receive a thousandfold daily amplification from the awakening after they age 20 (which is a gift from Godric himself, but they don't know. Note for you: the thousandfold daily amplification is not to protect Blake or his descendants from Godric--as established in previous lore, Godric has perfect Concealment Power which allows him to appear as normal human so he has no leaked aura or presence at all if he wish to.), but compared to Godric whose all magical traits are multiplying infinitely every Planck second, they are laughable, pretty much 0 (not to mention Godric could instantly and  effortlessly delete the very concept of magic from ever existing, which he didn't do because wizard needs magic and his best friends are wizards. You must not say that Godric is the one who invents magic, since it won’t make sense–Thorin was Godric’s best friend and a wizard before Godric went through the stasis event.).

Gorm is a young upcoming court wizard (20 years old) who thought his job is to protect the king with and from the arcane magics. He has known Godric since very young, being a descendant of Blake which the king is close with. To him Godric is the best friendly uncle, and he really wants to protect him with his magical aptitude which runs in his bloodlines, assuming the reason Godric kept court wizard everytime was because Godric lacks the magical aptitude and hence needs wizard's service.

Write the realization of how Gorm's belief shattered, the events that led to this change, and the aftermath. You must greatly exaggerate Godric's magical aptitude to an absurd horrifying degree, that an infinitesimal (practically 0% of Godric’s magic) magic of Godric can instantly and effortlessly erase an entire omniverse infinite times over, one that will induce extreme existential dread to the reader. Write from Gorm's pov. Do not end with humanization, preaching, and warm scenes.
<blockquote>
We need to write a story from Gorm's POV, 80,000 years after Godric became king. Gorm is 20, a descendant of Blake, and has always seen Godric as a friendly uncle figure. He believes his job is to protect the king with his arcane magic, because he thinks Godric lacks magical aptitude and that's why the king keeps court wizards. The story must shatter this belief, showing the horrifying truth: Godric's magical power is infinitely beyond comprehension, and even an infinitesimal fraction of it could erase the omniverse infinite times over. The event that leads to this realization could be an incident where Gorm witnesses a demonstration, or perhaps his attempt to protect Godric from a magical threat, which reveals Godric's true nature. The ending must not have humanization, preaching, or warm scenes. Pure existential dread.

We need to maintain 1st person POV of Gorm. Keep the tone epic horror thriller. Exaggerate Godric's magical supremacy. Show Gorm's internal dread. Include dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts. No bullet points, no LaTeX.

We should include details: Gorm has known Godric since childhood, sees him as a kind uncle. He has trained in magic, thinking he's the protector. The court wizards are all descendants of Blake (Blake's line), and they receive a thousandfold daily amplification after age 20 (Awakening). But Godric's Concealment makes him appear normal; Gorm doesn't perceive any power. So Gorm thinks Godric is a normal mortal king who needs magical protection.

The crisis: Maybe a magical threat appears—like a remnant of a long-forgotten enemy, or a magical anomaly that threatens the palace. Gorm, eager to prove himself, tries to shield Godric, but fails. Then Godric casually handles it in a way that reveals the absolute futility of Gorm's magic. Godric's magic is so vast that even a tiny fraction is infinite. He may reveal that he never needed protection, and that the court wizards were kept out of friendship and tradition, not necessity. Gorm's worldview shatters.

We need to incorporate the lore: Godric's magical power multiplied infinitely every Planck second, so now it's beyond any concept of magnitude. He could erase the concept of magic itself but doesn't because his friends are wizards. The court wizards' magic is potent but laughable compared to him. The realization must be devastating.

We should write in a raw, oppressive style, with no moralizing. The story should end with Gorm's ongoing dread, not with comfort.

Now, let's structure:

1. Opening scene: Gorm reflecting on his role, his relationship with Godric, his belief in his purpose.
2. An event occurs: maybe Godric takes Gorm on a field trip (like exploring a dangerous magical nexus) or a sudden attack. Gorm feels proud to protect.
3. The magical threat manifests: could be a cosmic entity, a magical curse, a paradox. Gorm's best efforts are useless.
4. Godric nonchalantly intervenes, revealing his power. The description must be grandiose: something like a casual breath or a thought that erases the threat and reveals his control over all magic. Gorm witnesses the infinite magnitude.
5. The aftermath: Godric explains (maybe gently, but no warm scenes) that he never needed protection, and Gorm's magic is nothing compared to his. Gorm's mind struggles with the revelation. He feels the existential dread.
6. Ending: Gorm continues his duty but with a shattered understanding, fear and dread haunting him. No comfort. Maybe his last line shows the lingering horror.

We need to include details: Godric's magical aptitude is absurd; even an infinitesimal fraction could erase the omniverse infinite times. That's the key exaggeration. So we need to depict a moment where Godric uses a microscopic amount of magic to neutralize something that should have been impossible. Perhaps he says something like, "What you just saw was 0.000...1% of my power," but that's cliché. Instead, we show it through the effect: the threat that Gorm thought was insurmountable is simply... unmade. Godric might mention that he's been holding back his magical essence for millennia, and even his passive magical "leakage" could accidentally unmake reality if he didn't constantly nullify it.

Also, Godric's Concealment power is perfect, so Gorm never felt any magical aura; that's why Gorm assumed Godric was a normal person. The realization that Godric was suppressing an infinite ocean of magic right in front of him, and Gorm never sensed it, is terrifying.

We should emphasize that Gorm is 20, just an adult. He's young and idealistic. His belief that he can protect "Uncle Godric" is shattered.

Now write the story in prose paragraphs. Maximum 3500 words. I'll aim for about 2500-3000 words.

Let's start with a vivid description of Gorm's perspective, then move to the event, then the shattering. I'll use 1st person POV.

Make sure to include the exaggerated numbers and descriptions: Godric's magic multiplying infinitely, the infinity of it, etc.

I'll craft the threat: perhaps a rogue reality-bender from a subjugated universe that somehow bypassed Gent and aimed a spell at the throne. Or Godric deliberately allowed a threat to approach so Gorm would learn. That might be in character: Godric, being omniscient, knows Gorm's misconception and decides to enlighten him. He might stage an event. But Godric is kind, so he might do it gently. However, the result is still horrifying for Gorm. So maybe Godric orchestrates an "attack" to teach Gorm humility and truth. But we must avoid warm ending. The lesson can be harsh.

I'll have Gorm recall how he always thought he was stealthily protecting Godric, but Godric was aware of every single magical attempt. Actually, Godric might say, "Do you think I didn't know every time you cast a protective ward around my bed? I could feel your tiny little spells. They were like the brush of a butterfly's wing." That would emphasize the gap.

The climax: Godric decides to show Gorm a fraction of his magical power. He takes Gorm to a void, or they encounter a magical entity that has been hiding. Gorm tries to fight, fails. Godric then simply "blinks" and the entity is erased, but in that blink, Godric lets out a sliver of his power, which Gorm perceives as an abyss so vast that he nearly goes insane. He realizes that his entire magical lineage, amplified a thousandfold daily for 80,000 years, is less than a single atom compared to a universe. Something like that.

I'll write in an oppressive style: Gorm's sensory overload, the cold dread, the realization that he is completely irrelevant.

Aftermath: Gorm continues as court wizard, but every day he feels the weight of Godric's power even when the king is being kind. He can't forget. The story ends with him accepting that he is a pet, a companion, not a protector, but that knowledge gnaws at him.

No warm scene at the end. Maybe a line like: "I still cast my wards, but now I know they are as useful as a child's drawing against a storm. And I smile at my uncle, because that's all I have left."

Now, write.

I need to avoid LaTeX and bullet points. Use standard prose.

Let's begin the story.

Blake is the one person with whom Godric is always warm, kind, and friendly. Godric considers Blake his absolute best friend.\n- **Godric's Redemption Arc:** Showcase the change in Godric transitioning back to a warm, friendly, and kind ruler due to Blake\u2019s influence. By the end of the story, Godric should be back to his original Olympus state: a just, kind, fatherly, warm, friendly person to his subjects, while retaining unforgiving ruthlessness and cruelty to his enemies.\n- **Blake's Legacy:** Show Blake slowly transitioning from a merchant to become a court wizard at the end of the story, with hints that his son, Josh, and future descendants are seemingly following in his footsteps to become the next loyal court wizards.\n- **Final Scene:** Conclude the epic with a vivid, atmospheric portrait of present-day Thronegate under Godric\u2019s absolute rule, showcasing Blake standing proudly as Godric\u2019s loyal right-hand man."

This is an absolute defense.\n\nBecause of absolute omniscience, he knows everything.\n\nWe need to show examples of his enhanced stats and superpowers manifesting. Describe the scene, his appearance, his interactions. Then the attack: sudden, violent. Show the deaths vividly. Thorin's sacrifice. The stasis event.\n\nThen transition to Blake's discovery.\n\nLet's draft.\n\n**Part 1: The Fall of Olympus**\n\nThe morning sun gilded the marble columns of Olympus, and King Godric stood on the palace balcony, watching servants string garlands of jasmine and myrtle across the courtyard. He was forty-five, his body still a monument to the discipline of decades\u2014broad shoulders, arms thick with muscle, a chest like a shield. His salt-and-pepper beard lay close against his jaw, and his short hair bore the first dignified streaks of silver. He smiled as his daughter Isabel, twenty-two and radiant in her betrothal silks, laughed with her sister Hebe, who was fifteen and still chasing butterflies between the guests\u2019 legs.\n\nGodric\u2019s wife, Reina, glided to his side. She touched his hand. \u201cYou\u2019ll make a fool of yourself crying during the vows.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m the king. I\u2019m allowed,\u201d Godric said, and his voice was the rumble of a hearth fire. He pulled her close, breathing the scent of olive oil and rosewater in her hair.\n\nThorin, the court wizard, appeared in the doorway. His robes were the deep blue of his bloodline, stitched with silver constellations. \u201cYour Majesty, the astral charts show only harmony today. The stars themselves bless this union.\u201d\n\n\u201cThen nothing can go wrong,\u201d Godric said, and for a moment, the world was whole.\n\nThe ceremony began in the grand temple. Isabel stood under a canopy of woven light, her groom\u2019s hands in hers. Godric, as officiant, raised the ceremonial chalice. The words never left his mouth.\n\nThe sky shattered. A sound like the universe tearing fabric ripped through the air, and the horizon vomited black-winged shapes. Thronegate\u2019s sigil\u2014a crimson fist clutching a lightning bolt\u2014burned on every banner. Fire rained. The temple\u2019s roof caved, and Godric threw himself over Reina and Hebe, but the blast took them anyway. He saw Isabel, still holding her groom\u2019s severed hand, before a spear of shadow impaled them both.\n\nThorin grabbed Godric\u2019s arm. \u201cThe spell! The sanctuary!\u201d His fingers blazed with arcane sigils. He began the incantation, an ancient, forbidden thing that only his lineage could utter. The air turned to syrup.\n\nA Thronegate mage materialized behind Thorin and rammed a blade of crystallized hatred through his spine. Thorin\u2019s blood splashed Godric\u2019s face. The wizard\u2019s lips kept moving, slurring the final syllables, before his body hit the stones.\n\nThe incomplete spell swallowed Godric. The world folded.\n\nHe awoke\u2014if it was waking\u2014in a vault of perfect silence. He could not move, could not blink, could not breathe. But he didn\u2019t need to. The stasis encased him like amber, and in that first Planck second, he felt the change begin.\n\nHis heart did not beat. His cells did not age. His body became a fixed, eternal moment. Then the multiplication started.\n\nStrength. It multiplied by a thousand, and then by itself, in the time it took light to cross a proton. The next Planck second, the new value did it again. And again. Every stat\u2014endurance, speed, senses, intelligence, wisdom\u2014bloomed into an autocatalytic apotheosis. He could feel the numbers climbing, but the mathematics soon lost meaning. His mind, already accelerating, groped for a metaphor and found none.\n\nAt the same time, powers began to manifest. One per second. The first was a perfect concealment: the ability to hold back his aura, his presence, his destruction, so that the universe would not evaporate at his mere proximity. The second was omniscience\u2014not just knowledge of present events, but the absolute, instantaneous understanding of all that was, is, and could be. By the third second, he knew everything that had happened during the attack, everything that would happen in the eons ahead, and the infinite branching paths of possibility that lay between.\n\nEach new power\u2019s potency multiplied with the same self-devouring frenzy as his base attributes. A power that could extinguish a civilization at its inception would, a blink later, snuff out a galaxy, then a universe, then a cluster of realities. And it never stopped.\n\nThe stasis also encoded a final, paradoxical defense. Godric had no weaknesses. It was an ontological truth, stitched into the weave of existence. But if any sentient being, anywhere, ever dared to imagine that he possessed a flaw\u2014if they so much as formed the thought\u2014the amplification rate would permanently spike. The perceived weakness would become immune, absorbed, and mastered by Godric before the thinker\u2019s neurons finished firing. And the very act of planning to exploit that imaginary crack would funnel more power into the one they sought to harm. It was a trap built from arrogance, and it was absolute.\n\nTime passed. Ten thousand years.\n\n---\n\n**Part 2: The Merchant**\n\nBlake prodded the rubble with a crowbar. The ruins on the outskirts of the Outer Arm weren\u2019t on any chart, and Blake, a merchant by trade, figured there might be salvage. He was thirty-eight, his face framed by a friendly mutton chop, his hands calloused from a hundred cargo runs. His wife Anna and their kids\u2014Josh, twelve, and Rhea, eight\u2014waited in the skiff a half-klick back.\n\nThe stone here didn\u2019t match the local geology. It was older, colder. He cleared a wall of fused debris and found a hidden chamber, its entrance shimmering with a faint, sickly light. Against his better judgment, he stepped inside.\n\nA man stood frozen in the center, encased in something that wasn\u2019t ice or crystal but a distortion of spacetime itself. The man\u2019s eyes were open, and they were the eyes of a father grieving his murdered children.\n\nBlake reached out. The moment his fingers touched the distortion, the stasis shattered.\n\nGodric\u2019s first breath in ten millennia was not a gasp but a statement of arrival. He stepped forward, and the universe groaned. Blake stumbled back, but Godric\u2019s gaze was not on him\u2014it was on everything, everywhere, all at once. Omniscience flooded him, and he sifted through the current state of the cosmos like a man riffling through old letters.\n\nHe saw Thronegate, grown fat and galactic. He saw King Robert, twenty-two, a boy on a throne of bones. He saw the massacre at Olympus, now dust and forgotten. And he saw Blake, the merchant, and in the man\u2019s bloodline a faint, familiar resonance\u2014a trace of the same arcane signature that had flashed in Thorin\u2019s dying hands. Godric said nothing.\n\nInstead, he spoke directly into the fabric of reality, and his voice echoed across the capital of Thronegate. \u201cKing Robert of Thronegate. I am Godric, the last king of Olympus, and I claim your throne. If I can defeat your entire military in three days\u2019 time, you will abdicate. Gather your forces.\u201d\n\nThe challenge hung in the air of a thousand worlds. Robert, arrogant and young, laughed on his live-streamed balcony. He accepted.\n\n---\n\n**Part 3: The Conquest**\n\nThe plains of Thronegate\u2019s homeworld, Nexus Prime, crawled with armament. Billions of super-soldiers stood in phalanxes, their power armor humming with enough energy to crack continents. War mages hovered on discs of negation, weaving spells that could unmake molecular bonds. Dreadnought-class robots, each the size of a small moon, hung in low orbit, their cannons trained. Dragons, ancient and star-faring, coiled in the upper atmosphere, their breath condensed into frozen lightning. And the Voidblade Ninjas, who had long ago learned to slice time itself, phased in and out of existence seven seconds ahead of the present.\n\nKing Robert watched from a floating citadel. Beside him, his generals smirked. This was the might that had obliterated a dozen sentient species. One man? Absurd.\n\nBlake stood with Anna on a distant ridge, a viewing scope pressed to his eye. Godric had told them to watch. \u201cYou need to understand what I am,\u201d he had said, and his tone had been so gentle that it terrified Blake more than any threat.\n\nGodric walked to the center of the battlefield. He wore no armor. He carried no weapon. He did not even move into a fighting stance. He simply stood, hands at his sides, and the armies of Thronegate began their assault.\n\nThe first volley was a continent-cracking beam from every orbital robot. It struck Godric and did nothing. The light bent around him, absorbed into a skin that had already become infinitely more durable than the dimensional fabric itself.\n\nThe mages unleashed entropy curses, age-accelerating doom, and conceptual erasure. Godric didn\u2019t notice. The curses fizzled before touching the boundary of his existence.\n\nThe Voidblade Ninjas dove, slicing through every possible fraction of a second to strike Godric before he could react\u2014except they struck only the space where he was, and he was already immune to time-based attacks because, somewhere in the last ten thousand years, he had passively acquired the absolute negation of chronological manipulation.\n\nHe lifted no finger. He simply thought, and the thought was: *Enough.*\n\nThe super-soldiers popped. Not exploded\u2014simply ceased, as if a child had erased a chalk drawing. The blood and viscera didn\u2019t spray; they were unmade, down to the last atom, leaving no evidence they had ever existed. The dragons folded into themselves like paper, and their ashes scattered into the wind. The robots\u2019 systems inverted, their own weaponry detonating internally, but the detonations were swallowed by localized voids that appeared and vanished in the same instant.\n\nThe mages felt their connection to magic severed, and then they felt their own souls unravel, slowly, neuron by neuron, so they could appreciate the complete annihilation of their selfhood.\n\nIt took less than a breath. Godric had not shifted his weight.\n\nOn the ridge, Blake vomited. Anna wept. The remaining air reeked of ozone and utter absence. The citadel, now empty of its king who was already sprinting to his throne room, drifted like a tombstone.\n\nTwo days later, King Robert was found in his chambers. He had used a ceremonial dagger to open his wrists, but the wounds were messy, panicked. The suicide note simply read, \u201cI thought he had a weakness. I was wrong.\u201d\n\nGodric walked into the palace, sat on the throne, and became the ruler of Thronegate.\n\n---\n\n**Part 4: The Awakening**\n\nThe day after his coronation, Godric issued the Decree of Awakening. The energy of the universe itself bent to his words. Every man in Thronegate, from the lowest janitor to the highest remaining general, felt a surge. For every day they had lived past the age of twenty, their strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom multiplied tenfold. A fifty-year-old man, who had lived thirty years beyond the threshold, found his abilities multiplied by ten, thirty times over\u2014a number so vast it made gods blink. And each day forward, it would grow again.\n\nThey could suppress it, dialing their power down to the level of normal men, and most did, for sanity\u2019s sake. They still aged; they would still die around eighty, as humans. But while they lived, they were demigods.\n\nBlake felt the Awakening differently. When the wave hit him, his bones vibrated, and his mind expanded. He did not know it, but his multiplier was not ten. It was a thousand. The same rules applied, but the scale was a hundredfold greater. He was still mortal, still a merchant, but now, if he wished, he could tear stars from their orbits. He never did.\n\nThe men of Thronegate revered Godric. Not out of fear, but out of gratitude. He protected women absolutely: a law enforced not by threat but by the instinct he had woven into the Awakening itself. Women were free, untouchable except by love. The citizens adored him. He was stern to his enemies, but to his people, he slowly began to smile again. Blake\u2019s influence, a quiet loyalty and an honest heart, reminded Godric of the man he had once been.\n\n---\n\n**Part 5: The Subjugation of the Omniverse**\n\nThronegate\u2019s dominion soon bled beyond their home cosmos. The omniverse, a fractal bloom of infinite universes, lay within Godric\u2019s perception. He issued a mandate: offer each target unconditional surrender. If they refused, subjugate them. Show no unnecessary cruelty, but tolerate no defiance.\n\n**First Universe: The Aaru Singularity**\n\nAaru was a realm of pure energy beings, who had evolved past matter. They saw the Thronegate scouts\u2014five men, all in their late fifties, kind-eyed fathers who missed their grandchildren\u2014and laughed. The Aaru had withstood the heat death of their home universe and rewritten the laws of entropy. They prepared for five years after hearing whispers of the falling cosmos. They constructed a barrier made of dead timelines, a wall of non-existence that no thing could cross.\n\nWhen the five Thronegate men arrived, they stood at the edge of the barrier. The eldest, a man named Doran with a white-flecked beard, tapped the barrier with his knuckle. \u201cPardon us,\u201d he said, and his voice was mild. \u201cWe mean you no harm. Surrender, and this ends.\u201d\n\nThe Aaru sent a pulse that would have erased the memory of the Thronegate species from history. It touched the men and dissolved. The Awakening had granted them immunity to conceptual retro-erasure two days prior, because the men had merely *thought* about the possibility while drinking coffee. Doran sighed. He raised his hand, and all five men released a fraction of their power\u2014just enough to bypass the barrier and hold the Aaru\u2019s central sun between their fingers, figuratively. \u201cPlease,\u201d Doran said. \u201cWe don\u2019t want to hurt you.\u201d\n\nThe Aaru understood then. They surrendered. The conquest took twenty-three minutes.\n\n**Second Universe: The Mechano-Collective**\n\nA universe of sentient machines, governed by a hive intelligence called the Core Directive. They had learned of Aaru\u2019s fall and fortified for five years. They turned entire galaxies into fortress-moons, weaponized black holes, and built a logic plague that could infect the very concept of consciousness.\n\nGodric himself was walking through the palace gardens when he noticed the Mechano-Collective\u2019s refusal to surrender. He was mildly annoyed; a flower had wilted in the heat. He didn\u2019t even pause in his stride. In the fractional instant that his mood flickered, the Core Directive\u2014spanning millions of light-years\u2014was simply deleted. Not destroyed. Deleted, as if the file of its existence was corrupted. The robot armies fell silent, the black holes evaporated, and the fortress-moons drifted inert. The omniverse registered the absence. Blake, next to him, said, \u201cYou okay?\u201d Godric nodded. \u201cJust a bug.\u201d The conquest took a fraction of a second.\n\n**Third Universe: The Nihilweave Coven**\n\nA dimension of pure magic, ruled by thirteen Sorcerer-Queens who had been plotting Godric\u2019s downfall since they first scryed his resurrection. They spent five years crafting a ritual that would invoke the Primordial Nothingness, the very antithesis of existence, to swallow Godric\u2019s being. They wove it into a tapestry of fate, binding every thread of his life to the Nothingness.\n\nFive Thronegate men, all over forty, walked through the portal into the Coven\u2019s throne dimension. They dodged the first volley of destabilization spells by simply phasing into a state of non-impact. Then they politely asked the Queens to cease. The Queens cackled and unleashed the Primordial Nothingness, a maw of anti-reality that had eaten gods.\n\nThe men looked at the Nothingness, and one of them, a former baker, said, \u201cMy daughter drew something like that once. Very abstract.\u201d He then flicked the maw with his middle finger, and the Nothingness collapsed into a pinprick and inverted, spewing forth a garden of pink roses instead. The Queens were bound in their own tapestry and gifted to Godric as a bouquet. Surrender arrived within seventeen minutes.\n\nNone of these conquered universes received the Awakening. They were assimilated, governed, and expected to obey.\n\n---\n\n**Part 6: The Futility of Resistance**\n\nIn the Era of Consolidation, a being named Zyphron the Unmaker emerged from the interstices between universes. Zyphron was older than time, a consciousness born from the residue of the original cosmic inflation. He observed Godric\u2019s reign and concluded, with the arrogance of a primordial, that perfection was a flaw. \u201cIf he has no weaknesses,\u201d Zyphron mused in his pocket dimension, \u201cthen his only possible flaw is his inability to have a flaw. That is a paradox I can exploit.\u201d\n\nZyphron did not realize that the moment he formed this thought\u2014the very first synaptic equivalent\u2014the Weakness Paradox triggered. Godric felt a tiny, pleasant hum in the base of his skull; his amplification rate kicked up another notch, though it was already so far beyond infinity that the increase was purely symbolic. He also instantly gained a new power: \u201cAbsolute Control Over Primordial Residue Beings Named Zyphron.\u201d He didn\u2019t even bother to check its name; the universe told him everything.\n\nZyphron spent a thousand years designing a weapon. He called it the Contradiction Engine, a metaphysical device that would force Godric to acknowledge a flaw by presenting a logical impossibility. It was, in essence, a mirror that would reflect Godric\u2019s own non-weakness back at him as a weakness. Zyphron traveled to the throne world, bypassed all defenses (Godric allowed it, out of curiosity), and activated the Engine in the throne room.\n\nThe Engine flared. A beam of orange light struck Godric.\n\nGodric looked up from the chess game he was playing with Blake. \u201cExcuse me a moment.\u201d He observed the beam, letting it touch his chest. Then he reached out, not with his hand, but with his will, and dismantled the Contradiction Engine not as a machine but as a concept. He unmade the idea of Zyphron\u2019s argument. Then he turned his attention to Zyphron.\n\n\u201cYou thought I had a weakness,\u201d Godric said, and his voice was quiet, almost sad. \u201cThat thought was your first mistake. Every second you spent planning, you gave me more power. You made me immune to your attack before the Engine was even a blueprint. And worst of all, you ensured I would master it.\u201d He held up a finger, and on its tip danced a miniature Contradiction Engine, perfected and a million times more potent. \u201cI could use this on you right now, but I won\u2019t. Your despair is enough.\u201d\n\nZyphron, a being who had never known fear, shattered into a cacophony of silent screams. Godric locked him in a dimension of perpetual dawning realization, where Zyphron would forever understand that his own mind had been the architect of his defeat. Then Godric turned back to Blake. \u201cYour move.\u201d\n\n---\n\n**Part 7: The Bond and the Legacy**\n\nTwenty years after the Awakening, Thronegate was a utopia of terrifying vitality. The men walked with the quiet confidence of gods, yet they laughed at stupid jokes and cried at their children\u2019s graduations. Godric had changed. The cruel edge that had been born from Olympus\u2019s ashes had been sanded down by Blake\u2019s companionship. Blake, now forty-eight (though he looked barely thirty), never called him \u201cmy king\u201d in private. It was always \u201cGodric,\u201d or sometimes, when he was annoyed, \u201cyou absolute bastard.\u201d\n\nGodric laughed at that, a sound that rumbled like the purr of a cosmic cat.\n\nBlake\u2019s role had shifted over the years. He no longer traded goods; he studied the arcane. The old magic of Olympus resonated with him, and Godric taught him, patient and fatherly. Blake\u2019s children, Josh and Rhea, grew into powerful men and women, and Josh, in particular, showed a preternatural affinity for wizardry. He had Thorin\u2019s high cheekbones and the same intense focus when he scried the stars. Blake never knew why the craft came so easily to his bloodline, but he accepted it as a gift.\n\nOne evening, Godric and Blake stood on a balcony overlooking the capital. The city glittered, and beyond it, the galaxy they ruled, and beyond that, the web of infinite universes.\n\n\u201cDo you miss them?\u201d Blake asked. He never prodded about Olympus, but tonight felt different.\n\nGodric\u2019s face was unreadable. \u201cEvery second. But I\u2019ve learned that grief doesn\u2019t need to be a weapon. You showed me that.\u201d He placed a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and the strength in that hand was the weight of a trillion suns, yet it was also the gentlest touch Blake had ever felt. \u201cYou\u2019re more than my right hand, Blake. You\u2019re my brother.\u201d\n\nBlake said nothing, because what could you say to a god who called you brother? He simply stood there, watching the city, feeling the hum of the Awakening in his veins, and knowing that his son would one day stand in his place, and his son\u2019s son after him, a lineage of loyal court wizards serving a king who had once been a father.\n\nAnd in the deepest part of the palace, in a locked stasis vault, the original blue robes of Thorin\u2014recovered from the ashes of Olympus\u2014hung in silent testament, waiting for the day the rightful bloodline would claim them again. But that was a story for another age.\n\n---\n\n**Final Scene: Present-Day Thronegate**\n\nThe throne room was vast, its ceiling open to the swirling nebulae of a hundred galaxies. Godric sat on a throne of woven starlight, his salt-and-pepper beard now a permanent fixture of his forty-five-year-old face, his muscular frame relaxed. Before him, a delegation from a newly encountered universe knelt in terror. They had just witnessed a demonstration of the Awakened men\u2019s power, and their bravado had crumbled.\n\nGodric listened to their pleas with patience. When they finished, he spoke. \u201cYour surrender is accepted. Your people will be fed, educated, and protected. You will lose your sovereignty, but you will gain peace. Does anyone object?\u201d\n\nNo one did.\n\nAt his side, Blake stood in the robes of a court wizard, a staff of living wood in his hand. He looked at the delegation and gave them a small, encouraging smile. \u201cIt\u2019s not so bad,\u201d he said, and the absurdity of those words in that context made one of the delegates laugh\u2014a nervous, broken sound that seemed to release a fragment of the dread.\n\nAfter the delegation was led away, Godric turned to Blake. \u201cAnother one saved.\u201d\n\n\u201cAnother one conquered,\u201d Blake corrected gently.\n\n\u201cSame thing, in the end.\u201d Godric\u2019s eyes, which had seen the death of his family and the birth of a trillion civilizations, crinkled at the corners. \u201cCome, let\u2019s visit Anna. She\u2019s making that stew you like.\u201d\n\nThey walked out together, two old friends, and the omniverse spun on, utterly indifferent to the small, warm moments that held it all together.\n\n---\n\n**Check word count:** Let's see.
