                {
                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "The morning sun gilded the marble columns of Olympus, and King Godric stood on the palace balcony, watching servants string garlands of jasmine and myrtle across the courtyard. He was forty-five, his body still a monument to the discipline of decades\u2014broad shoulders, arms thick with muscle, a chest like a shield. His salt-and-pepper beard lay close against his jaw, and his short hair bore the first dignified streaks of silver. He smiled as his daughter Isabel, twenty-two and radiant in her betrothal silks, laughed with her sister Hebe, fifteen and still chasing butterflies between the guests\u2019 legs.\n\nGodric\u2019s wife, Reina, glided to his side. She touched his hand, her fingers cool from the morning air. \u201cYou\u2019ll make a fool of yourself crying during the vows.\u201d\n\n\u201cI\u2019m the king. I\u2019m allowed,\u201d Godric said, his voice a rumble like a hearth fire. He pulled her close, breathing the scent of olive oil and rosewater in her hair.\n\nThorin, the court wizard, appeared in the doorway. His robes were the deep blue of his bloodline, stitched with silver constellations that seemed to shift when you didn\u2019t look directly at them. \u201cYour Majesty, the astral charts show only harmony today. The stars themselves bless this union.\u201d\n\n\u201cThen nothing can go wrong,\u201d Godric said, and for a moment, the world was whole.\n\nThe ceremony began in the grand temple. Isabel stood under a canopy of woven light, her groom\u2019s hands in hers. Godric, as officiant, raised the ceremonial chalice. The words never left his mouth.\n\nThe sky shattered. A sound like the universe tearing fabric ripped through the air, and the horizon vomited black-winged shapes. Thronegate\u2019s sigil\u2014a crimson fist clutching a lightning bolt\u2014burned on every banner. Fire rained. The temple\u2019s roof caved inward, and Godric threw himself over Reina and Hebe, but the blast took them anyway. He saw Isabel, still holding her groom\u2019s severed hand, before a spear of shadow impaled them both through the spine, pinning their bodies together like a grotesque ornament.\n\nThorin grabbed Godric\u2019s arm, his grip desperate. \u201cThe spell! The sanctuary!\u201d His fingers blazed with arcane sigils, and he began the incantation, an ancient, forbidden thing that only his lineage could utter. The air turned to syrup, thick and unbreathable. A Thronegate mage materialized behind Thorin and rammed a blade of crystallized hatred through his spine. Thorin\u2019s blood splashed Godric\u2019s face, hot and coppery. The wizard\u2019s lips kept moving, slurring the final syllables, before his body hit the stones with a wet thud.\n\nThe incomplete spell swallowed Godric. The world folded.\n\nHe awoke\u2014if it was waking\u2014in a vault of perfect silence. He could not move, could not blink, could not breathe. But he didn\u2019t need to. The stasis encased him like amber, and in that first Planck second, he felt the change begin.\n\nHis heart did not beat. His cells did not age. His body became a fixed, eternal moment. Then the multiplication started.\n\nStrength. It multiplied by a thousand, and then by itself, in the time it took light to cross a proton. If his base strength had once let him lift a boulder, then after one Planck second it was the power to juggle mountains. Another Planck second, and mountains became continental plates. Then moons. Then worlds. The next Planck second, it multiplied again\u2014by a thousand, and by the new value itself. The numbers lost all meaning. His mind, already accelerating, groped for a metaphor and found only the sensation of standing at the edge of an abyss that had no bottom, and then falling upward.\n\nEvery stat\u2014endurance, speed, senses, intelligence, wisdom\u2014bloomed into the same autocatalytic apotheosis. His endurance became such that the concept of \u201cdamage\u201d would need to be rewritten to apply to him. His speed rendered the idea of \u201cinstant\u201d sluggish. His senses unfolded across dimensions he had never known existed, tasting the vibration of strings in the quantum foam.\n\nAt the same time, powers began to manifest. One per second. The first was a perfect concealment: the ability to hold back his aura, his presence, his destruction, so that the universe would not evaporate at his mere proximity. The second was omniscience\u2014not just knowledge of present events, but the absolute, instantaneous understanding of all that was, is, and could be. By the third second, he knew everything that had happened during the attack, everything that would happen in the eons ahead, and the infinite branching paths of possibility that lay between.\n\nEach new power\u2019s potency multiplied with the same self-devouring frenzy as his base attributes. A power that could extinguish a civilization at its inception would, a blink later, snuff out a galaxy, then a universe, then a cluster of realities. And it never stopped.\n\nThe stasis also encoded a final, paradoxical defense. Godric had no weaknesses. It was an ontological truth, stitched into the weave of existence. But if any sentient being, anywhere, ever dared to imagine that he possessed a flaw\u2014if they so much as formed the thought\u2014the amplification rate would permanently spike. The perceived weakness would become immune, absorbed, and mastered by Godric before the thinker\u2019s neurons finished firing. And the very act of planning to exploit that imaginary crack would funnel more power into the one they sought to harm. It was a trap built from arrogance, and it was absolute.\n\nTime passed. Ten thousand years.\n\n---\n\nBlake prodded the rubble with a crowbar. The ruins on the outskirts of the Outer Arm weren\u2019t on any chart, and Blake, a merchant by trade, figured there might be salvage. He was thirty-eight, his face framed by a friendly mutton chop, his hands calloused from a hundred cargo runs. His wife Anna and their kids\u2014Josh, twelve, and Rhea, eight\u2014waited in the skiff a half-klick back.\n\nThe stone here didn\u2019t match the local geology. It was older, colder. He cleared a wall of fused debris and found a hidden chamber, its entrance shimmering with a faint, sickly light that made his fillings ache. Against his better judgment, he stepped inside.\n\nA man stood frozen in the center, encased in something that wasn\u2019t ice or crystal but a distortion of spacetime itself. The man\u2019s eyes were open, and they were the eyes of a father grieving his murdered children.\n\nBlake reached out. The moment his fingers touched the distortion, the stasis shattered. The universe groaned\u2014a subsonic shudder that rippled through the local stars and made Anna clutch the kids in sudden, inexplicable terror. Godric stepped forward, and the groan ceased instantly. He pulled his aura inward, a cloak of absolute self-restraint, and the omniverse steadied.\n\nOmniscience flooded him. He sifted through the current state of the cosmos like a man riffling through old letters. He saw Thronegate, grown fat and galactic. He saw King Robert, twenty-two, a boy on a throne of bones. He saw the massacre at Olympus, now dust and forgotten. And he saw Blake, the merchant, and in the man\u2019s bloodline a faint, familiar resonance\u2014a trace of the same arcane signature that had flashed in Thorin\u2019s dying hands. Godric said nothing.\n\nInstead, he spoke directly into the fabric of reality, and his voice echoed across the capital of Thronegate. \u201cKing Robert of Thronegate. I am Godric, the last king of Olympus, and I claim your throne. If I can defeat your entire military in three days\u2019 time, you will abdicate. Gather your forces.\u201d\n\nThe challenge hung in the air of a thousand worlds. Robert, arrogant and young, laughed on his live-streamed balcony. He accepted.\n\n---\n\nThe plains of Thronegate\u2019s homeworld, Nexus Prime, crawled with armament. Billions of super-soldiers stood in phalanxes, their power armor humming with enough energy to crack continents. War mages hovered on discs of negation, weaving spells that could unmake molecular bonds. Dreadnought-class robots, each the size of a small moon, hung in low orbit, their cannons trained. Dragons, ancient and star-faring, coiled in the upper atmosphere, their breath condensed into frozen lightning. And the Voidblade Ninjas, who had long ago learned to slice time itself, phased in and out of existence seven seconds ahead of the present.\n\nKing Robert watched from a floating citadel, a goblet of wine untouched in his hand. Beside him, his generals smirked. This was the might that had obliterated a dozen sentient species. One man? Absurd.\n\nBlake stood with Anna on a distant ridge, a viewing scope pressed to his eye. Godric had told them to watch. \u201cYou need to understand what I am,\u201d he had said, and his tone had been so gentle that it terrified Blake more than any threat.\n\nGodric walked to the center of the battlefield. He wore no armor. He carried no weapon. He did not even move into a fighting stance. He simply stood, hands at his sides, and the armies of Thronegate began their assault.\n\nThe first volley was a continent-cracking beam from every orbital robot. It struck Godric and did nothing. The light bent around him, absorbed into a skin that had already become infinitely more durable than the dimensional fabric itself.\n\nThe mages unleashed entropy curses, age-accelerating doom, and conceptual erasure. Godric didn\u2019t notice. The curses fizzled before touching the boundary of his existence, like raindrops on a sun.\n\nThe Voidblade Ninjas dove, slicing through every possible fraction of a second to strike Godric before he could react\u2014except they struck only the space where he was, and he was already immune to time-based attacks because, somewhere in the last ten thousand years, he had passively acquired the absolute negation of chronological manipulation. The ninjas found themselves arrested mid-slice, their blades frozen, their own reversed time snapping back and trapping them in a loop of instants that never completed.\n\nHe lifted no finger. He simply thought, and the thought was: *Enough.*\n\nThe super-soldiers popped. Not exploded\u2014simply ceased, as if a child had erased a chalk drawing. The blood and viscera didn\u2019t spray; they were unmade, down to the last atom, leaving no evidence they had ever existed. The dragons folded into themselves like paper, their scales crackling, their roars cut off as their lungs collapsed into a point. The robots\u2019 systems inverted, their own weaponry detonating internally, but the detonations were swallowed by localized voids that appeared and vanished in the same instant, leaving only a hiss of displaced vacuum.\n\nThe mages felt their connection to magic severed, and then they felt their own souls unravel, slowly, neuron by neuron, so they could appreciate the complete annihilation of their selfhood. One mage, an elder with three centuries of power, managed a scream before his vocal cords dissolved.\n\nIt took less than a breath. Godric had not shifted his weight. The silence that followed was a physical weight, a pressure on the eardrums of every witness. On the ridge, Blake vomited onto the rocks. Anna wept, her hands shaking as she clutched her own arms. The remaining air reeked of ozone and utter absence. The citadel, now empty of its king who was already sprinting to his throne room, drifted like a tombstone.\n\nTwo days later, King Robert was found in his chambers. He had used a ceremonial dagger to open his wrists, but the wounds were messy, panicked. The suicide note simply read, \u201cI thought he had a weakness. I was wrong.\u201d\n\nGodric walked into the palace, sat on the throne, and became the ruler of Thronegate.\n\n---\n\nThe day after his coronation, Godric issued the Decree of Awakening. The energy of the universe itself bent to his words. Every man in Thronegate, from the lowest janitor to the highest remaining general, felt a surge. For every day they had lived past the age of twenty, their strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom multiplied tenfold. A fifty-year-old man, who had lived thirty years beyond the threshold, found his abilities multiplied by ten, thirty times over\u2014a number so vast it made gods blink. And each day forward, it would grow again.\n\nThey could suppress it, dialing their power down to the level of normal men, and most did, for sanity\u2019s sake. They still aged; they would still die around eighty, as humans. But while they lived, they were demigods.\n\nBlake felt the Awakening differently. When the wave hit him, his bones vibrated, and his mind expanded. He did not know it, but his multiplier was not ten. It was a thousand. The same rules applied\u2014he could suppress it, he would age and die\u2014but the scale was a hundredfold greater. He was still mortal, still a merchant, but now, if he wished, he could tear stars from their orbits. He never did.\n\nThe men of Thronegate revered Godric. Not out of fear, but out of gratitude. He protected women absolutely: a law enforced not by threat but by the instinct he had woven into the Awakening itself. Any man who even thought of harming a woman felt his own strength invert, a blinding feedback of agony that corrected the impulse instantly. Women walked free, untouchable except by love. The citizens adored him. He was stern to his enemies\u2014a swift, merciless disintegration for those who broke his laws\u2014but to his people, he slowly began to smile again. Blake\u2019s influence, a quiet loyalty and an honest heart, reminded Godric of the man he had once been.\n\n---\n\nThronegate\u2019s dominion soon bled beyond their home cosmos. The omniverse, a fractal bloom of infinite universes, lay within Godric\u2019s perception. He issued a mandate: offer each target unconditional surrender. If they refused, subjugate them. Show no unnecessary cruelty, but tolerate no defiance.\n\nThe first universe they faced was Aaru, a realm of pure energy beings who had evolved past matter. They saw the Thronegate scouts\u2014five men, all in their late fifties, kind-eyed fathers who missed their grandchildren\u2014and laughed. The Aaru had withstood the heat death of their home universe and rewritten the laws of entropy. They had learned of the falling cosmos and prepared for five years. They constructed a barrier made of dead timelines, a wall of non-existence that no conceivable thing could cross.\n\nWhen the five Thronegate men arrived, they stood at the edge of the barrier. The eldest, a man named Doran with a white-flecked beard, tapped the barrier with his knuckle. \u201cPardon us,\u201d he said, his voice mild. \u201cWe mean you no harm. Surrender, and this ends.\u201d\n\nThe Aaru sent a pulse meant to erase the memory of the Thronegate species from history. It touched the men and dissolved, because the Awakening had granted them immunity to conceptual retro-erasure two days prior, when the men had merely *thought* about the possibility while drinking coffee. Doran sighed. He raised his hand, and all five men released a fraction of their power\u2014just enough to bypass the barrier and hold the Aaru\u2019s central sun between their fingers, figuratively. \u201cPlease,\u201d Doran said. \u201cWe don\u2019t want to hurt you.\u201d\n\nThe Aaru\u2019s light dimmed\u2014their species\u2019 equivalent of weeping. They surrendered. The conquest took twenty-three minutes.\n\nThe second universe was the Mechano-Collective, a realm of sentient machines governed by a hive intelligence called the Core Directive. They had learned of Aaru\u2019s fall and fortified for five years. They turned entire galaxies into fortress-moons, weaponized black holes, and built a logic plague that could infect the very concept of consciousness.\n\nGodric himself was walking through the palace gardens when he noticed the Mechano-Collective\u2019s refusal to surrender. He was mildly annoyed; a flower had wilted in the afternoon heat. He didn\u2019t even pause in his stride. In the fractional instant that his mood flickered, the Core Directive\u2014spanning millions of light-years\u2014was simply deleted. Not destroyed. Deleted, as if the file of its existence was corrupted. The robot armies fell silent; their sensors went dark and their limbs locked. The black holes evaporated in a quiet whisper of Hawking radiation that should have taken eons. The fortress-moons drifted inert, cold tombs. The omniverse registered the absence and filled the void with indifferent silence. Blake, next to him, said, \u201cYou okay?\u201d Godric nodded. \u201cJust a bug.\u201d The conquest took a fraction of a second.\n\nThe third universe was the Nihilweave Coven, a dimension of pure magic ruled by thirteen Sorcerer-Queens. They had been scrying Godric\u2019s resurrection since the moment he awoke, and they spent five years crafting a ritual to invoke the Primordial Nothingness, the very antithesis of existence, to swallow his being. They wove it into a tapestry of fate, binding every thread of his life to the Nothingness.\n\nFive Thronegate men, all over forty, walked through the portal into the Coven\u2019s throne dimension. The air there smelled of crushed violets and burnt sugar, and the sky was a weeping wound of purple light. They dodged the first volley of destabilization spells by simply phasing into a state of non-impact, their forms flickering like old film. Then they politely asked the Queens to cease.\n\nThe Queens cackled and unleashed the Primordial Nothingness\u2014a maw of anti-reality that had eaten gods and the concepts they represented. The men looked at the Nothingness, and one of them, a former baker named Kell, said, \u201cMy daughter drew something like that once. Very abstract.\u201d He flicked the maw with his middle finger, and the Nothingness collapsed into a pinprick and inverted, spewing forth a garden of pink roses that wilted almost immediately in the alien atmosphere. The Queens were bound in their own tapestry and gifted to Godric as a bouquet. Surrender arrived within seventeen minutes.\n\nNone of these conquered universes received the Awakening. They were assimilated, governed, and expected to obey.\n\n---\n\nIn the Era of Consolidation, a being named Zyphron the Unmaker emerged from the interstices between universes. Zyphron was older than time, a consciousness born from the residue of the original cosmic inflation. He observed Godric\u2019s reign and concluded, with the arrogance of a primordial, that perfection was a flaw. \u201cIf he has no weaknesses,\u201d Zyphron mused in his pocket dimension, \u201cthen his only possible flaw is his inability to have a flaw. That is a paradox I can exploit.\u201d\n\nZyphron did not realize that the moment he formed this thought\u2014the very first synaptic equivalent\u2014the Weakness Paradox triggered. Godric felt a tiny, pleasant hum in the base of his skull; his amplification rate kicked up another notch, though it was already so far beyond infinity that the increase was purely symbolic. He also instantly gained a new power: \u201cAbsolute Control Over Primordial Residue Beings Named Zyphron.\u201d He didn\u2019t even check the name; the universe told him everything.\n\nZyphron spent a thousand years designing a weapon. He called it the Contradiction Engine, a metaphysical device that would force Godric to acknowledge a flaw by presenting a logical impossibility. It was, in essence, a mirror that would reflect Godric\u2019s own non-weakness back at him as a weakness. Zyphron traveled to the throne world, bypassed all defenses (Godric allowed it, out of idle curiosity, having foreseen every step eons before), and activated the Engine in the throne room.\n\nThe Engine flared. A beam of orange light struck Godric.\n\nGodric looked up from the chess game he was playing with Blake. \u201cExcuse me a moment.\u201d He observed the beam, letting it touch his chest. Then he reached out, not with his hand, but with his will, and dismantled the Contradiction Engine not as a machine but as a concept. He unmade the idea of Zyphron\u2019s argument, unraveling it like a knotted thread. Then he turned his attention to Zyphron.\n\n\u201cYou thought I had a weakness,\u201d Godric said, and his voice was quiet, almost sad. \u201cThat thought was your first mistake. Every second you spent planning, you gave me more power. You made me immune to your attack before the Engine was ever a blueprint. And worst of all, you ensured I would master it.\u201d He held up a finger, and on its tip danced a miniature Contradiction Engine, perfected and a million times more potent, its light rotating through colors Zyphron had no names for. \u201cI could use this on you right now, but I won\u2019t. Your despair is enough.\u201d\n\nZyphron, a being who had never known fear, shattered into a cacophony of silent screams that warped the local spacetime into knots of eternal agony. Godric locked him in a dimension of perpetual dawning realization\u2014a sealed bubble where Zyphron would forever relive the moment he understood that his own mind had been the architect of his defeat. Then Godric turned back to Blake. \u201cYour move.\u201d\n\n---\n\nTwenty years after the Awakening, Thronegate was a utopia of terrifying vitality. The men walked with the quiet confidence of gods, yet they laughed at stupid jokes and cried at their children\u2019s graduations. Godric had changed. The cruel edge born from Olympus\u2019s ashes had been sanded down by Blake\u2019s companionship. Blake, now fifty-eight, never called him \u201cmy king\u201d in private. It was always \u201cGodric,\u201d or sometimes, when he was annoyed, \u201cyou absolute bastard.\u201d\n\nGodric laughed at that, a sound that rumbled like the purr of a cosmic cat.\n\nBlake\u2019s role had shifted over the years. He no longer traded goods; he studied the arcane. The old magic of Olympus resonated with him in ways he couldn\u2019t explain\u2014as if his fingers remembered patterns his mind had never learned. Godric taught him, patient and fatherly, and Blake absorbed it with an ease that bordered on inheritance. His son, Josh, now a tall man of thirty-two, showed a similar gift, with high cheekbones and an intense focus when he scried the stars\u2014features that, had any portrait of Thorin survived, might have sparked a question. But none did.\n\nOne evening, Godric and Blake stood on a balcony overlooking the capital. The city glittered with lights that were not electric but bioluminescent, grown from the flora of a conquered universe. Beyond it, the galaxy they ruled, and beyond that, the web of infinite realities.\n\n\u201cDo you miss them?\u201d Blake asked. He never prodded about Olympus, but tonight felt different.\n\nGodric\u2019s face was unreadable. \u201cEvery second. But I\u2019ve learned that grief doesn\u2019t need to be a weapon. You showed me that.\u201d He placed a hand on Blake\u2019s shoulder, and the strength in that hand was the weight of a trillion suns, yet it was also the gentlest touch Blake had ever felt. \u201cYou\u2019re more than my right hand, Blake. You\u2019re my brother.\u201d\n\nBlake said nothing, because what could you say to a god who called you brother? He simply stood there, watching the city, feeling the hum of the Awakening in his veins\u2014a thousandfold gift he never abused\u2014and knowing that his son would one day stand in his place, and his son\u2019s son after him, a lineage of loyal court wizards serving a king who had once been a father.\n\nIn the deepest part of the palace, in a locked stasis vault, the original blue robes of Thorin\u2014recovered from the ashes of Olympus by Godric\u2019s secret will\u2014hung in silent testament, waiting for a day when the rightful bloodline might claim them again. But that was a story for another age.\n\n---\n\nThe throne room was vast, its ceiling open to the swirling nebulae of a hundred galaxies, their light captured and tamed by an Awakened architect\u2019s whim. Godric sat on a throne of woven starlight, his salt-and-pepper beard a permanent fixture of his forty-five-year-old face, his muscular frame relaxed. Before him, a delegation from a newly encountered universe knelt in terror. They had just witnessed a demonstration of the Awakened men\u2019s power\u2014a display that had shattered their bravado like glass\u2014and now they shook, their six-lobed eyes leaking a fluid that smelled like copper.\n\nGodric listened to their pleas with patience. When they finished, he spoke. \u201cYour surrender is accepted. Your people will be fed, educated, and protected. You will lose your sovereignty, but you will gain peace. Does anyone object?\u201d\n\nNo one did.\n\nAt his side, Blake stood in the robes of a court wizard\u2014a deep blue, stitched with silver constellations that shifted subtly in the corner of one\u2019s eye. His staff was of living wood, a gift from a botanical dimension, and it hummed with a quiet, protective warmth. He looked at the delegation and gave them a small, encouraging smile. \u201cIt\u2019s not so bad,\u201d he said, and the absurdity of those words in that context made one of the delegates emit a sound that might have been a laugh\u2014a nervous, broken noise that seemed to release a fragment of the dread.\n\nAfter the delegation was led away, Godric turned to Blake. \u201cAnother one saved.\u201d\n\n\u201cAnother one conquered,\u201d Blake corrected gently.\n\n\u201cSame thing, in the end.\u201d Godric\u2019s eyes, which had seen the death of his family and the birth of a trillion civilizations, crinkled at the corners. \u201cCome, let\u2019s visit Anna. She\u2019s making that stew you like.\u201d\n\nThey walked out together, two old friends, and the omniverse spun on, utterly indifferent to the small, warm moments that held it all together. The legacy of Thorin, unwitting and unspoken, continued in the man who now joked beside the king, and in the generations that would follow, bound by a loyalty that had outlasted the stars."

                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "My knuckles have been cracked and bleeding for eight years. The skin never heals right because I keep picking at the scabs while I sit beside Rogr\u2019s bed, watching him twitch through another nightmare he can\u2019t describe. The bedroom smells of old sweat and the lavender oil I rub into his temples\u2014not because it helps, but because the routine gives my hands something to do besides shake.\n\nRogr\u2019s eyes open. They are the color of river stones, and they used to crinkle when he laughed. Now they dart like beetles trapped under glass, and when he speaks, his voice is a broken whisper that repeats the same phrase he said the day he came home from the palace.\n\n\u201cSo heavy,\u201d he says. \u201cSo heavy.\u201d\n\nI remember that day. He had been selected as one of the delegates from the newly assimilated universe of Quelthorn, a proud people who had expected a monster. He was nervous about meeting the king, but I told him the truth: Godric is good. Godric is just. Godric is the reason our children can play in the streets without fear and our elderly can walk at night without a weapon. I had told Rogr, \u201cYou\u2019ll see. He\u2019s not what the rumors say.\u201d\n\nWhen Rogr returned, he couldn\u2019t walk. His legs had given out in the antechamber, and the palace guards\u2014Awakened men with the quiet, terrifying calm of living weapons\u2014had carried him home on a stretcher made of solidified light. His eyes were open the whole time, but he wasn\u2019t there. He was somewhere else, somewhere I couldn\u2019t follow.\n\nThe healers could find nothing wrong. The physicians ran their scans and shook their heads. The psychics probed his mind and fled the room, one of them vomiting into a potted fern. \u201cThe king\u2019s presence,\u201d one whispered at me, her pupils blown wide. \u201cHe was\u2026 displeased.\u201d\n\nDispleased. That was the word she used. I couldn\u2019t understand it. Godric is the kindest ruler Thronegate has ever known. He visits schools. He remembers the names of foot soldiers. He once paused a military campaign to help an old woman find her lost cat. The idea that he could be displeased with a minor delegate from a forgettable world seemed absurd. And even if he were, so what? A king\u2019s displeasure is a political inconvenience, not a sentence to a living death.\n\nBut Rogr\u2019s body told a different story. In the first year, he lost thirty pounds. He stopped sleeping except in microbursts that left him gasping. He developed a twitch in his left hand that no nerve block could quiet. He soiled himself whenever someone mentioned the throne. I bathed him and changed his sheets and told myself that time would heal whatever this was, because time is supposed to heal everything, and because Godric\u2019s kingdom is a place where suffering is meant to be temporary.\n\nOur son Pete was four when it started. He\u2019s twelve now, and he doesn\u2019t remember his father before the breaking. To Pete, Dad has always been the man in the corner who flinches at ceiling lights and mutters about weight. Pete loves Godric with the pure, uncomplicated devotion of a child raised under absolute protection. Every year on Coronation Day, Pete draws pictures of the king with a crayon crown and asks me to hang them on the refrigerator. I hang them. I smile. And then I go into the bedroom and hold Rogr\u2019s hand while he screams soundlessly at the wallpaper.\n\nI tried to fix him. I tried everything.\n\nFirst, the Aural Harmonizers from the Vestra Nebula. They attune brainwaves to frequencies that dissolve traumatic imprints. I paid a fortune in credits I didn\u2019t have, and when the Harmonizer touched Rogr\u2019s forehead, the device emitted a single, pure note\u2014and then crumpled into a ball of molten metal, as if it had tried to analyze a trauma so vast that its own circuitry chose suicide over comprehension. The technician who sold it to me refunded my money without being asked. \u201cI don\u2019t know what happened to your husband,\u201d she said, \u201cbut that machine has never failed before. It\u2019s like it chose to die.\u201d\n\nSecond, the Mnemonic Weavers, a species of telepathic spider-creatures who disentangle painful memories. They took one look at Rogr and teleported themselves back to their home dimension, leaving behind a note that read only: \u201cWe are not qualified.\u201d\n\nThird, the taboo: I consulted a Void Scryer, a being that lives in the cracks between universes and sells forbidden knowledge. It spoke through a mouth that wasn\u2019t a mouth and said, \u201cYour husband brushed against the hem of infinity. The king\u2019s displeasure was a fraction so small it barely existed, but the universe must obey even the ghost of his mood. Your husband\u2019s mind wasn\u2019t broken by the king. It was broken by the realization of how small he truly is. There is no cure for knowing you are nothing.\u201d\n\nI didn\u2019t believe it. I couldn\u2019t. A fraction so small it barely existed? A ghost of a mood? That was enough to turn my husband into a husk? What kind of god does that? And why would a good king allow it?\n\nBut I kept those thoughts locked behind my teeth. Because to voice them would be to question Godric himself, and I loved Godric too much to do that. I loved him for the safe streets, for the food in my pantry, for the way he had outlawed the old brutalities that used to plague Thronegate\u2019s women. I loved him for my son\u2019s intact innocence. How do you hold gratitude and horror in the same heart? You don\u2019t. You just let them tear at each other until you\u2019re numb.\n\nOn the tenth anniversary of Rogr\u2019s collapse, a man came to our door. He was old, maybe sixty, with a friendly mutton chop and a weariness in his shoulders that spoke of decades of service. He wore a court wizard\u2019s robes\u2014blue, stitched with silver constellations that moved when I wasn\u2019t looking directly at them. I knew him instantly. Everyone knows Blake, the king\u2019s right hand. The only person who can scold a being that can unmake galaxies with a thought.\n\n\u201cMrs. Vell,\u201d he said. \u201cMy name is Blake. I\u2019m here to apologize.\u201d\n\nHe sat at our kitchen table, and he told me the truth. A joke. A stupid, offhand comment he had made to Godric eight years after the coronation. \u201cThe new delegates think you\u2019re a tyrant,\u201d Blake had said. \u201cYou should play along for a bit. Just a tiny bit. Scare them a little before you show them who you really are.\u201d\n\nAnd Godric, who loves Blake like a brother, had agreed.\n\nBlake\u2019s voice cracked as he spoke. \u201cHe held back everything, Rosa. He thought he was being gentle. He literally cannot comprehend what even a shred of his presence does to a mortal. He thought it would be\u2026 a little unsettling. Like a stern headmaster. He didn\u2019t know.\u201d He repeated it like a prayer for absolution. \u201cHe didn\u2019t know.\u201d\n\nMy first instinct was rage. Ten years. Ten years of washing my husband\u2019s body, of listening to him whimper, of watching my son grow up without a father. All because of a prank. A prank.\n\nMy second instinct was to throw Blake out. But I didn\u2019t. Because Blake was crying. The most powerful wizard in the omniverse, second only to Godric himself, had tears running into his mutton chop, and his hands trembled around the cup of tea I hadn\u2019t offered him.\n\n\u201cHe told me yesterday,\u201d Blake said. \u201cGodric mentioned it casually. \u2018Remember that prank? That one delegate never quite bounced back. Mortals are so fragile.\u2019 He said it like he was talking about a broken toy. He genuinely believes in mortal resilience because he used to be one of us, ten thousand years ago, and he survived worse. He thinks we\u2019re all just\u2026 tougher than we are. He doesn\u2019t understand the gap.\u201d\n\nBlake lifted his head. \u201cI can ask him to fix it. He will, if I ask. But I won\u2019t do it without your permission.\u201d\n\nPermission. To let the man whose casual disgust had shattered my husband into our home. To let him touch Rogr again.\n\nI sent Blake away. I told him I needed to think. That night, I sat beside Rogr\u2019s bed and held his hand. \u201cThey want to bring him here,\u201d I whispered. \u201cThe king. He can fix you. He says it was an accident.\u201d\n\nRogr didn\u2019t respond. His eyes were fixed on the ceiling, and his lips moved silently. \u201cSo heavy.\u201d\n\nPete came in. \u201cMom? Was that Blake? The Blake?\u201d His face was alight with hero worship. \u201cDoes the king know about Dad? Is he going to help?\u201d\n\nI looked at my son, who had every poster of Godric ever printed, who had once dressed as the king for a school play and delivered a speech about justice and mercy that had made the teachers weep. And I thought: if I say no, what am I preserving? A shell. A memory of a man who is already gone.\n\n\u201cYes,\u201d I said. \u201cHe\u2019s going to help.\u201d\n\nI didn\u2019t call Blake. I didn\u2019t send a message. I simply said the word \u201cyes\u201d aloud in my kitchen at 3:14 in the morning, and Godric appeared.\n\nHe didn\u2019t stride through a portal or materialize in a pillar of light. He was simply there, as if the air had always been shaped like him and I was only now permitted to notice. The kitchen didn\u2019t brighten or dim. The temperature didn\u2019t change. But every cell in my body screamed at once, a primitive animal shriek that bypassed my rational mind and lodged in my spine.\n\nHe was beautiful. That was the worst part. He looked exactly like his statues: late forties, perfectly muscular, a salt-and-pepper beard and kind eyes. His presence wasn\u2019t menacing. It was warm. Fatherly. But beneath that warmth was a pressure, a sense that I was standing next to an ocean and had suddenly realized the water had no bottom, only a lightless descent into something that could swallow all the stars and not burp.\n\nPete, standing in the hallway, gasped and fell to his knees. Not from pain. From awe.\n\nGodric smiled at him. \u201cHello, young man. You\u2019ve grown since your last school play.\u201d\n\nPete made a sound that was half sob, half laugh. The king knew about the school play.\n\nThen Godric looked at me, and I understood, in that moment, exactly what had happened to Rogr. Because even though Godric was radiating nothing but kindness, my mind was still trying to process the sheer scale of him. He was holding back everything\u2014everything, an infinite, self-contained universe of power\u2014but my mortal senses could still perceive the echo of what he was holding back, the way you can feel the pressure behind a dam even if the water isn\u2019t touching you. And if this was him being gentle, then what Rogr had seen\u2014a fraction of a sliver of manufactured displeasure\u2014was a hell I could not fathom.\n\nI didn\u2019t bow. I couldn\u2019t move. Godric didn\u2019t seem to mind.\n\n\u201cBlake told me,\u201d Godric said, and his voice was genuinely sad. \u201cI miscalculated. I thought I was being amusing. I forget, sometimes, what it felt like to be small.\u201d\n\nHe walked past me into the bedroom. I followed on legs that didn\u2019t feel like my own. He stood at the foot of Rogr\u2019s bed and looked down at my husband, who had started to tremble the moment Godric entered the house. The twitching had stopped. Now Rogr was utterly still, like a rabbit in a hawk\u2019s shadow.\n\n\u201cDon\u2019t be afraid,\u201d Godric said to him. \u201cI\u2019m going to undo what I did.\u201d\n\nHe lifted no hand. He spoke no incantation. He didn\u2019t even furrow his brow in concentration. He simply\u2014decided.\n\nRogr\u2019s body arched once, a smooth, graceful curve, and then settled back onto the mattress. The color returned to his cheeks in a flush that made him look younger than he had in a decade. The hollows under his eyes filled. His breathing deepened. The perpetual sheen of sweat vanished. He looked, in the span of a single heartbeat, like a man who had never spent a single second in distress. More than that: he looked like a man who had been sculpted from the platonic ideal of health. His skin glowed. His hair thickened. Even his fingernails seemed to grow a shade pinker.\n\nBut his eyes\u2014when they opened, they were still river stones, and they still carried the memory. \u201cRosa,\u201d he said. His voice was hoarse but clear. \u201cI saw something. I saw the size of everything, and the size of me.\u201d\n\n\u201cI know,\u201d I said. \u201cIt\u2019s over.\u201d\n\nHe sat up. He looked at his hands as if seeing them for the first time. Then he looked at Godric, and instead of terror, his face broke into the first smile I had seen in ten years. \u201cThank you,\u201d he said.\n\nGodric nodded. \u201cTell Blake I owe him one.\u201d\n\nJust like that. A decade of my husband\u2019s suffering, undone because a friend asked nicely.\n\nI should have felt only joy. And I did feel joy\u2014a wild, frantic joy that made me weep and clutch Rogr\u2019s hand and kiss his knuckles until he laughed. But beneath it was something else. A cold, quiet horror that crept into my bones and made a home there.\n\nThe Harmonic Harmonizer had melted. The Weavers had fled dimensions. The Scryer had told me there was no cure. I had spent years, years, bankrupting myself and degrading my sanity, trying every conceivable method to heal my husband. All of it, hopeless. Useless. The universe itself had deemed Rogr\u2019s condition immutable.\n\nAnd Godric had fixed it in less time than it takes to blink. Not because he tried hard. But because he simply existed, and existence obeys him.\n\nWhat did that make me? What did that make all my effort? A joke. A cosmic joke, and I was the punchline.\n\nGodric turned to me, and I realized he had heard that thought. Of course he had. He hears everything.\n\n\u201cYou\u2019re not a joke, Rosa,\u201d he said, and his voice was so gentle it hurt. \u201cYou fought for your husband with everything you had. That\u2019s not nothing. That\u2019s everything.\u201d\n\nHe offered me compensation. Not a token. He offered me a planet\u2014a literal planet, a garden world in the Jeweled Nebula, with oceans of warm silk and forests that sang in four-part harmony. He offered me enough wealth to make my grandchildren\u2019s grandchildren richer than queens. He offered me a permanent seat on his advisory council, a voice in the governing of the omniverse.\n\nI shook my head. \u201cNo. I don\u2019t want anything.\u201d\n\nHe didn\u2019t push. He didn\u2019t insist. He simply nodded, as if my refusal was as valid as any choice could be. \u201cAs you wish,\u201d he said, and that respect\u2014that absolute, unquestioning respect for my tiny, insignificant will\u2014was somehow the most terrifying thing of all. Because it confirmed what the cold part of my mind already knew: this being, who could force the universe to obey him, chose instead to let me refuse him. The power wasn\u2019t just in his ability to command. It was in his restraint. He could have overwhelmed my will as easily as he overwhelmed Rogr\u2019s trauma, but he chose not to, and that choice was itself a demonstration of supremacy so profound that my mind skittered off it like a stone off ice.\n\nGodric left. One moment he was there; the next, the kitchen was just a kitchen again, and the air was just air. Pete rushed to his father\u2019s bed, and they embraced, and I stood in the doorway and smiled until my face hurt.\n\nThe days that followed were strange. Rogr became the neighborhood celebrity. Neighbors stopped by to marvel at his recovery, to touch his hand as if he were a relic. He told the story of Godric\u2019s mercy to anyone who would listen, and his voice was always reverent. The king had saved him. The king had apologized. The king was good.\n\nAnd he was right. Godric *was* good. I believed that with my whole heart. I still do. I go to temple on Coronation Day, and I sing the hymns, and I mean every word. When I see Godric\u2019s face on the broadcasts, I feel a swell of love and gratitude that is entirely genuine.\n\nBut I also feel the cold thing. It lives behind my sternum now, a splinter of ice that never melts. Every time I look at my husband\u2019s healthy face, I see the ten years I lost. Every time I hear Pete talk about the king, I remember that the same being who fixed my husband is the one who broke him\u2014on a whim, for a joke. Every time I close my eyes, I feel the pressure of that presence, the knowing that I am a speck in a cosmos that god uses as a joke book.\n\nLast week, I was at the market when I saw them. Godric and Blake, walking together through the crowd. The citizens parted around them like water around stones. No one bowed; Godric had decreed that unnecessary. But everyone\u2019s eyes followed him, shining with adoration.\n\nI caught a fragment of their conversation.\n\n\u201cWe should do that again,\u201d Godric said. \u201cThe prank. Maybe tone it down even more this time. There\u2019s a new batch of delegates from a realm that thinks I breathe fire. It could be hilarious.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s face went through five expressions in half a second. \u201cAbsolutely not. Are you insane? Do you remember what happened last time?\u201d\n\n\u201cYes, but I fixed it,\u201d Godric said, and he sounded genuinely puzzled by Blake\u2019s tone. \u201cOne trauma, one fix. Net zero.\u201d\n\n\u201cNet zero\u2014Godric, it took ten years of that man\u2019s life!\u201d\n\n\u201cI know. But I fixed it.\u201d Godric paused. \u201cI\u2019ll hold back more this time. Maybe ninety-nine point nine-nine-nine\u2014actually, I\u2019ll add a few more nines. Make it so mild it\u2019s barely above total absence. They\u2019ll just feel a little chill. No permanent damage.\u201d\n\nBlake dragged a hand down his face. \u201cI\u2019m going to regret this conversation.\u201d\n\n\u201cIs that a yes?\u201d\n\n\u201cIt\u2019s a \u2018shut up, Godric.\u2019\u201d\n\nThe king laughed. It was a warm, genuine laugh, the kind that makes you want to laugh along with him. And I, standing twenty feet away with a bag of vegetables in my hand, felt the cold splinter sharpen and twist.\n\nBecause they were joking about it. The thing that had destroyed my husband for a decade, that had ground my life into dust, was a conversation topic between them. Not out of malice\u2014they weren\u2019t cruel. But because the gap between them and us is so vast that our suffering registers as an inconvenience to be easily corrected, and the correction absolves the cause. They genuinely don\u2019t understand why we can\u2019t just move on.\n\nAnd here\u2019s the part that makes me sick: I still love them. Both of them. Blake, for his guilt and his apologies and his tears at my kitchen table. Godric, for his mercy and his smile and the way he healed my husband with a thought. Even now, typing this, I am grateful. I am grateful to the being who let me suffer for a decade because he thought a prank was funny, and who fixed it only because his best friend told him to.\n\nI am grateful, and I am terrified, and I don\u2019t know how to stitch those two truths together without tearing myself apart.\n\nThis morning, Rogr woke up singing. He made breakfast. He kissed me on the forehead and said, \u201cI feel like I\u2019ve been asleep for ten years. But I\u2019m awake now.\u201d\n\nI kissed him back. I told him I loved him. And I didn\u2019t tell him about the cold thing, or the conversation at the market, or the way my hands still shake when I think about the sheer, effortless weight of Godric\u2019s presence.\n\nSome things, I think, are meant to be carried alone."

                    "text": "I\u2019ve served at Godric\u2019s side for twelve years, and I still can\u2019t get my legs to stop shaking when the air turns heavy like this. The battleground is a pocket realm, a flat disc of compressed reality floating in the void between universes, and standing beside the throne, I can see them all. The resistance. The big one. The one they\u2019ve been building for eighty centuries, give or take a few millennia, right under our noses\u2014except not really under our noses, because Godric always knew. He let them. He excluded them from Gent\u2019s passive annihilation with a thought so casual that I don\u2019t think he even blinked. He was curious. That\u2019s the word he used. Curious.\n\nI look at the horde stretching across the horizon of this dead space, and I want to laugh. Not because it\u2019s funny. Because laughter is the only valve my brain has left. There are trillions of them. The numbers they\u2019ve assembled aren\u2019t just astronomical; they\u2019re narrative-breaking. Battlefleets made from the crystallized dreams of dead creator gods. Legions of abstract-concept assassins, the kind that kill ideas so thoroughly that the universe forgets they ever existed. Wizards who have dissected the source code of reality and written their own patches. The Eschaton Engine\u2014a weapon that looks like a throbbing star collapsing in reverse, built from the harvested final moments of a million universes. The Paradox Swordsman, whose blade has tasted the blood of Time, Death, and the very concept of Loss. The Omni-Mage Coalition, billions strong, their magic woven into a single spell that hums so violently it makes the multiverse\u2019s foundation creak. And the Voidborn King leading his Armada of Eternal Night, his crown a singularity, his warships space-time predators that hunt and consume causality.\n\nAnd that\u2019s just the named ones. The ones with reputations. The ones who\u2019ve published manifestos. Behind them are the uncounted: reality-benders who can blink galaxies to dust, omega-psykers whose thoughts can rewrite the laws of physics, warriors clad in the skins of outer gods, and beasts with maws full of dead timelines. Godric watches the assembly with the mild interest of a man observing an anthill. He\u2019s seated, one leg crossed over the other, his salt-and-pepper beard catching the light of a dying universe he\u2019d pocketed earlier for ambiance. He looks like a handsome, muscular father waiting for his kid\u2019s school play to start. His posture is relaxed. His eyes are kind. And that\u2019s the part that always gets me\u2014the genuine, unfiltered kindness. He\u2019s not faking it. The same warmth that makes him personally apologize to palace cooks when he\u2019s late for dinner is there, right now, as the most powerful coalition in all of existence prepares to annihilate him.\n\n\u201cThey\u2019ve been planning for so long,\u201d I say, my voice coming out flatter than I intended. \u201cYou really think they have a shot?\u201d\n\nGodric turns to me, his expression thoughtful. \u201cProbably not. But I want to see if Gent breaks a sweat. The poor thing has never had to try. I\u2019ve coddled it.\u201d\n\nI almost choke. Gent. That\u2019s what he named his passive defense aura. It stands for Gentle, which is the most ironic thing he\u2019s ever done, because Gent is anything but gentle. Gent is a sentient, omnipresent, omniscient force that is functionally Godric\u2019s metaphysical body heat\u2014the excess energy his existence just kind of leaks. It\u2019s infinitely weaker than he is, which is the part that shatters glass in my head if I think about it too long. Infinitely. And those are the words Godric uses. \u201cInfinitely weaker.\u201d As if that puts any kind of scale on it. Gent could unmake the omniverse in the time it takes me to form the thought, and yet, compared to Godric, it\u2019s the equivalent of a single lukewarm breath in a hurricane of absolute power. But Gent is also fiercely, obsessively subservient. It loves Godric. It would do anything for him. And that includes holding back 99.99...% of its true power\u2014an infinite recursion of nines, a decimal that never resolves, a fraction so infinitesimal that any mind attempting to calculate it would just slide off into madness\u2014because Godric asked nicely.\n\nThe assault begins without warning. One moment, the resistance is a tableau; the next, the universe screams.\n\nThe Eschaton Engine fires first. Its causality collapse doesn\u2019t travel; it\u2019s simply there, a sphere of absolute negation erupting at every single point of space Godric occupies. The sphere freezes, then shivers, and Gent doesn\u2019t even flicker. Instead, the Engine\u2019s own causality collapses inward, reversing with an added twist. The weapon becomes a prison for its creators. I watch as the master engineers of the Engine\u2014tall, crystalline beings whose minds existed across twelve dimensions\u2014find themselves trapped inside their own device\u2019s activation loop. They dissolve, reform, and dissolve again, their bodies peeling apart in layers of screaming light, their consciousness preserved perfectly so they feel every instant of the eternal recursion. Their screams are so high-pitched that the local space-time rips open like wet paper, and Gent patches the tears with a lazy pulse of warmth before they can spread.\n\nThe Paradox Swordsman moves next, and his speed is such that he should have been here a full second before he started. His blade, the Absolute Denial, cuts through concepts\u2014it has killed Hope, severed Fate, and once, rumor says, it nicked the idea of Godric\u2019s mortality before Godric even had a body. He swings it in a strike that should retroactively erase Godric from the moment of his birth. The blade shatters. Not against a shield; against the simple, passive fact of Gent\u2019s existence. And then the swordsman learns what it means to be denied. Gent doesn\u2019t kill him. It erases him from the timeline, but it does it slowly, cell by cell, while keeping his awareness stretched across the entire span of his life so he experiences his own un-becoming from every angle. I see his face\u2014handsome, angular, the kind of face that has never known defeat\u2014contort into pure, incomprehensible horror as his body fades from the future backward, the past backward, and the present all at once. His mouth opens, but the sound is swallowed by the void.\n\nThe Omni-Mage Coalition unleashes their grand spell: a tapestry of rewritten laws that should turn Godric\u2019s infinite power against itself, a magical paradox that uses his own existence as fuel. The spell touches Gent and inverts. Every single mage across those billions feels their connection to magic yanked inside out. Their bodies become conduits not for power but for pain, and their magic transforms into a physical substance\u2014molten lead, mixed with razor blades and sentient acid. They don\u2019t just die; they melt into puddles of screaming flesh that retain consciousness, their minds merged into a composite shriek that Gent eventually silences by absorbing the puddles into itself, leaving nothing but a faint, lemony scent of ozone.\n\nThe Voidborn King, whose crown is a singularity, roars a command, and his Armada of Eternal Night opens fire with black hole cannonballs. Each one tears through the fabric of reality, and each one is simply\u2026 stopped. They hang in space, suspended by a thought from Gent, and then the King\u2019s own flagship, a dreadnought the size of a solar system, is pinched between two of Gent\u2019s metaphorical fingers\u2014except the fingers are made of the King\u2019s own shadow, turned against him. The ship crumples. The King, a being who has never known physical sensation, suddenly feels every atom of his body being compressed into an infinitely dense point. But Gent doesn\u2019t let him die. It expands him back, slowly, so he can gasp one ragged breath of non-existent air, then crushes him again. Each cycle, I can feel the King\u2019s despair ripple through the pocket realm like a seismic wave, and Gent absorbs that too, as if tasting it.\n\nThe rest of the trillions? They don\u2019t even get a moment. Gent is omnipresent. That means it\u2019s everywhere at once, even inside their minds, their histories, their potential futures. It simply decides, and they die. Some implode. Some dissolve into static. Some are eaten by their own shadows. Some are un-written from the narrative of existence so completely that even the memory of their names vanishes from the brains of their allies\u2014except Godric allows me to remember, because he knows I\u2019d feel left out otherwise. The whole thing takes a fraction of a second. Actually, less. A sliver of an instant. The battlefield goes from an impossible army to empty stillness, not even a smear of blood or a fleck of ash. Gent, diligent as always, cleans up. The space shines. The stars outside the pocket realm twinkle with restored innocence. Even the ozone smell is replaced by something like fresh laundry.\n\nMy legs give out. I don\u2019t fall\u2014I\u2019m too proud for that\u2014but I stumble, catching myself on the arm of Godric\u2019s throne. The cold metal bites my palm, grounding me. I can\u2019t stop staring at the emptiness. A trillion voices, snuffed, and the only remnant is a faint hum in the air that I recognize as Gent\u2019s equivalent of a pleased purr.\n\nGodric sighs. It\u2019s a small sound, but it lands like a thunderclap. \u201cGent,\u201d he says, and the hum shifts to something contrite. \u201cYou held back, right? I asked you to.\u201d\n\nA mental nod, somehow visible in the way the air pressure shifts.\n\n\u201cYou held back to the infinite nines?\u201d\n\nAnother nod. Slightly defensive.\n\nGodric pinches the bridge of his nose. \u201cThen why didn\u2019t they even get close enough to make you try? I wanted you to at least feel a little resistance. A scratch. A tickle.\u201d\n\nThe air around us thickens with something that feels suspiciously like an aura pouting. My mouth goes dry. He\u2019s scolding it. The most terrifying force I have ever witnessed, the thing that just obliterated the ultimate resistance without me even needing to blink, and he\u2019s scolding it like a puppy that tore up a slipper.\n\n\u201cWe\u2019ll work on it,\u201d Godric says, and his tone is that of a father promising extra practice. \u201cI\u2019ll teach you restraint. Real restraint. This isn\u2019t your fault. I haven\u2019t been a good teacher.\u201d\n\nI almost laugh. I almost scream. Restraint. This is the king who, three weeks ago, accidentally erased a galaxy because he thought too hard about what to have for lunch. He restored it immediately, of course\u2014snap of the fingers, everything back, not a single soul aware they\u2019d been briefly non-existent\u2014but the fact remains: Godric doesn\u2019t know restraint. Not really. He tries, and his trying is a cosmic horror because even his attempts at gentleness are apocalyptically overpowered. And now he\u2019s going to teach an equally overpowered aura how to be gentle. It\u2019s like watching two black holes try to dance ballet. Someone\u2019s going to get spaghettified.\n\nBut the true horror hits me as I keep looking at the pristine emptiness. The resistance. Eighty centuries of preparation. Millennia of scheming in secret, gathering power, gathering allies, amassing weapons that could individually unmake creation. And in those eighty centuries, something else was happening. Something that makes my brain feel like it\u2019s trying to fold itself into a tesseract.\n\nGodric\u2019s power multiplies. Not by a thousand anymore\u2014that\u2019s a cute, ancient number, a relic from the Stasis Event ten thousand years ago before the Weakness Paradox got triggered so many times that the multipliers themselves multiplied into beyond incalculable mathematics. Now? Every Planck second, his strength, his speed, his intelligence, his every stat and every single apocalyptic superpower\u2014and he has been gaining a new one every second for ten thousand years\u2014multiplies infinitely. Not by a finite number. The increase is infinite, and that new infinite value then multiplies by itself, and the process repeats, forever, at a speed so small that the concept of \u201cduration\u201d loses meaning.\n\nDo you understand what that means? The Godric sitting next to me right now could, with a stray idle thought, erase an infinite number of copies of the Godric from one Planck second ago. They would be infinitely weaker than him\u2014still gods beyond gods, but to the current Godric, they\u2019d be like candles next to the entire thermal output of a universe. And that was one Planck second. The resistance spent eighty centuries planning. That\u2019s about 2.4 x 10^53 Planck seconds, give or take, and in every single one of those intervals, Godric\u2019s power ballooned by an infinite exponent of itself. By the time they launched their first attack, the Godric they\u2019d built their strategies against was so far gone that the comparison wasn\u2019t even a joke anymore; it was a fundamental category error. It\u2019s like a bacterium mustering its entire existence to fight the heat death of the cosmos and then realizing, in its final moment, that the cosmos itself is just a thought in a being that has already moved on to another thought.\n\nI don\u2019t know the math. I can\u2019t hold it. But I feel it, a crawling dread in my bone marrow, a knowledge that the longer anyone fights Godric, the more futile it becomes, because the goalposts aren\u2019t moving\u2014they\u2019re accelerating at a speed that makes light look like a paralyzed snail. Their preparation didn\u2019t just fail; it actively fed his amplification through the Weakness Paradox, and their delays turned an already infinite gap into something even more impossible. They never had a chance. They made the chance smaller by trying.\n\nAnd then Gent evolves.\n\nIt happens without a sound, without a flash. One moment, the aura is a passive warmth, the metaphysical equivalent of a loyal dog at Godric\u2019s side. The next, I feel it stretch, not outward but *conceptualward*. It doesn\u2019t just guard Godric now; it begins un-creating the very possibility of threat. I watch, my throat closing, as the remnants of the resistance\u2019s existence\u2014the causal ripples they left, the memory traces in the fabric of the multiverse\u2014are gently, lovingly erased. Not violently. Not even coldly. With a tenderness that is infinitely more terrifying than any malice. It retcons them from the book of reality, leaving only the pages Godric allows us to keep. And it does this retroactively, across all timelines, all dimensions, all potentialities, with the soft hum of a lullaby. The Voidborn King\u2019s entire species, which had existed for eons, is suddenly a thing that was never born. The Paradox Swordsman\u2019s legend dissolves, and the concept of Absolute Denial itself becomes a blank spot in the cosmic index. Even the Eschaton Engine\u2019s creators are unmade from the memory of invention, their blueprints turned to void. Gent cleans so thoroughly that the omniverse shifts and settles around the absence, and no one notices except me, because Godric wants me to notice, and I wish he didn\u2019t.\n\nGodric claps his hands together. \u201cWell! Look at that.\u201d His voice is full of genuine, heartwarming pride. He beams at the empty space where Gent\u2019s new presence pulses. \u201cDid you see that, Tim? He evolved! All on his own. I didn\u2019t even prompt him.\u201d\n\nHe turns to the air, and for a second, I see his face soften in exactly the same way my father\u2019s did when I first cast a successful fire spell as a kid. \u201cGood boy, Gent. Such a good boy. I\u2019m so proud of you.\u201d\n\nThe air glows. The warmth intensifies, and I could swear I feel something nuzzle against Godric\u2019s hand, even though his hand doesn\u2019t move. Gent is preening. Pleading for more praise. The most omnipotent defense mechanism in all of existence, evolved to un-write the concept of danger itself, is wiggling like a puppy that just figured out how to sit on command.\n\nAnd I\u2014I can\u2019t breathe. My chest is full of ice. My mind is tearing itself apart trying to hold two realities at once: the fatherly, kind king who truly, deeply loves his people, and the predator whose exhalation just unmade the greatest threat the omniverse had ever assembled. The love is real. The pride is real. And that\u2019s the part that makes me want to curl into a ball and never uncurl. He doesn\u2019t understand. He cannot understand. He believes in mortal resilience because he was mortal once, in an age so distant that the stars he knew have all burned out, and he thinks we can just\u2026 take it. He thinks a bit of existential horror is like a stubbed toe\u2014painful, but you walk it off. And because he\u2019s so utterly, incalculably beyond us, he\u2019ll never know how wrong he is.\n\nI\u2019m still standing when Godric rises from the throne and stretches, muscles shifting under his tunic, his salt-and-pepper beard framing a satisfied smile. \u201cWell, that was refreshing. Gent needed the exercise. Come on, Tim. I\u2019m in the mood for that spicy soup from the Verdant Sphere. My treat.\u201d\n\nHe starts walking toward the portal, and Gent, the ever-loyal, folds the pocket realm behind us with the care of a mother tucking in a child. I follow, as I always do, because I am his court wizard, and because I love him. Because despite everything, he is good. He is just. He is the reason I can walk home to my family without fear. And I will serve him until the day I die, and my loyalty is absolute, and my mind will never, ever stop screaming."

Opening scene: Leon standing in the void where the battle takes place, next to Godric. He describes the omniverse's gathered forces, the ultimate weapon, the sheer scale of sacrifice. He feels a mix of awe for Godric and a creeping dread.\n\n2. The attack: The entire omniverse channels its power into a single point, a weapon forged from the death of infinite multiverses, wielded by the last survivors. Godric tells Leon, \"Watch this.
